  4. So I just received my Gillette ProGlide and shaving cream yesterday as a bzzagent client, to try out and review, and got my first chance to use it today. I have to say that I've used my Gillette M3 Power for years now and have been quite happy. Whenever I'd tried to move to a 4-blade system, they've always clogged up or been harder to clean, so there I've stayed. However, this new razor was a pleasure to use. Let's take a closer look at the bundle below. First of all, the razor. I was a little let down that I received the Non-powered razor as I've been using a powered razor for years, and love how smooth of a shave I get from them. The simple vibrating seems to really help with the overall experience of the shave, in my opinion. But, I am willing to overlook this for the sake of the review. Afterall, there is a power option for this razor if I decide that I like it enough to change. So the first, and most obvious change in this razor over other razors I've used is the swivel head. When manually moving the head, it does move very smoothly and easily. Considering that I've always been very careful to shave straight however, I was still a bit unsure how much of a difference this would really make. The handle to the razor feels very solid in my hand, being of a metal design. Adds some good weight that feels good in my hands. Good rubberized grips keep it from shifting or sliding. Also has the same simple push-pop removable head that we've become accustom to with other razors. Secondly, the shaving gel. The design of the bottle is very sleek. Easy to hold thanks to the matte feel to the bottle, and a rubberized bottom to help avoid rusting, as advertised on the bottle itself. That will take some time to test and I dont' leave mine sitting in water anyhow. Also advertised, is the no-mess nozzle. I was a bit skeptical at first as all that I've seen usually have a little bit of mess. And this one touting the twist to lock top, I figured that's about where it ended. More on that in a bit. The final bit of advertising on the bottle, I'll state right off that I like. On the side of the bottle is a thin window into the inside of the bottle. This is designed so that as you near the last half of supply, you can monitor as you are about to run out. This is a simple, but great addition that I wish that other manufacturers to pick up on. Great idea! So, now that we've gone over the basics of the items received, let's get to the shaving. I put this razor to the test a bit more, as I haven't shaved in a few days and so stubble has gotten a bit longer. Probably could have trimmed it first. *shrug* First thing I noticed was in applying the gel. The nozzle truly is mess free, and there was not the slightest bit of gel left on the nozzle after applying to my hand. it comes out at a pretty high pressure and really sprays a nice solid stream into my hand. Could probably shoot it across the room at someone, if I really wanted! :p With the higher pressure, I hadn't realized just how much I had expelled, so after applying to my face I had quite a bit of leftover. So, note to self next time. Small squirts. As expected, the gel felt cool and smooth going on. foamed up perfectly and the scent that I ordered was fresh and strong. But not too strong to irritate while shaving. As I began to shave, I was trying to make note of the swivel head, to see if it was really doing anything as I shaved. Although I can't say that I really noticed any swivel on the razor, and kept shaving straight as I usually do, I can say that it felt very smooth on my face and no areas of extra pressure I may notice with my regular razor. This most likely will make a difference in the razor burn feel that I get occasionally, especially down on my throat. I haven't noticed any after shaving here. One simple light pass and it has left my face well shaved. This was to be expected, but a bit more impressive as I hadn't shaved in a couple of days, as I'd previously noted.Rinsing the razor was pleasant as well, as I noticed not the slightest clogging as I'd expected with the 4 blades, and longer stubble. Felt like a good, clean shave. Overall, I was very impressed with this razor. I cannot currently see any negatives, outside of the fact that I think that if I continue using this razor, I shall be sure to pick up the Powered option however that's probably just personal preference. Initial impression on these items, definitely impressed and know that I'll most likely look for these shaving gels for replace..if nothing more than simply the window on the bottle. The absolutely no mess at this point is nice as well. The razor? I'll use this one without power for awhile, and decide how to proceed later. My Rating on this razor set? Probably a good 9 out of 10.

  17. I received both the Gillette Fusion Proglide Razor and 2-in-1 Shave Gel as part of an evaluation program. Here is my review...<br /><br />Wow, what a smooth shave! I've always laughed at the increasing number of blades in razors. This coming from someone who has been using his 2-bladed Gillette Excel since he can remember. The Excel has always provided a clean, close shave but with the downside of raw, reddish, irritated skin. It was a consequence I accepted as just part of shaving.<br /><br />Now, I'm eating my crow, with relish! The Gillette Fusion ProGlide with its 5 blades cuts cleanly and smoothly, whether I went with the grain or against (I usually do with first, then against on a second pass--everyone says go with but how can you get a close shave that way?). I felt no nicks, pulls, or cuts, and my face never felt raw. Applying Nivea After Shave Balm post shave, I did not feel any burn like I normally do. It's a good indication to me that my skin wasn't raked raw.<br /><br />I also compared the ProGlide razor to my Norelco Coolskin 7775X electric shavor. I put in the new HQ8 replacement blades since the original HQ177 blades are no longer available. I found the HQ8 blades to be better than the HQ177: smoother and closer in my opinion. Many reviewers contend otherwise (I shave in the shower so perhaps others have different results because of different circumstances). I love my Norelco because it provides a smooth, close shave without irritation. But it takes time and a good number of passes to achieve the results. So in comparison to the Norelco, the ProGlide was equally smooth and close without the multiple passes and extra time.<br /><br />The smooth shave really won me over but there were other great features about the ProGlide razor. The articulating razor head was excellent at pivoting itself around cheek bones and jaw lines. As a result, the razor stayed glued to my skin for a close shave. Weight and grip of the razor felt solid and good, not plasticky or cheap. Love the dark chrome and metal feel.<br /><br />I haven't come to any conclusions on the FlexBall yet. I shaved without a mirror and didn't notice whether the FlexBall pivoted side to side as it was intended to. Perhaps it did to help navigate the contours of my face or perhaps it didn't and is just a marketing gimmick. I'll have to shave again, this time in front of a mirror to judge properly.<br /><br />The ProGlide razor isn't perfect and here is its one flaw: the razor head is big. How can it not be with 5 blades? Gillette did a fantastic job of keeping the blades thin, thinner than the Excel blades, but they do still command a bit of real estate. They are also slightly wider than the Excel. So all of this translates to some difficulty shaving hair at and around the upper lip. I could only shave with the grain here and very carefully at that. The razor just felt a little tall for that small region. I also had slight difficulty under the jaw where the skin dips. Again, because the razor head is relatively large and not easily maneuvered there. I can see myself improving my technique with practice so this isn't a major issue, just an issue for my first time out.<br /><br />I normally shave once a week, even with the Norelco. My skin usually requires a break before the next shave and shaving short stubble after a few days usually results in pain. But I am optimistic enough with the ProGlide experience that I will try shaving more frequently. If I am able to shave more often, then I can be content with a close enough shave rather than needing that super close shave. In fact, I would prefer to shave more often just so I don't look so scruffy by the week's end. Here's hoping...<br /><br />I shaved several more times with the ProGlide and can tell the razor blades dulling after about 3 shaves. Your mileage might vary since each person's hair/stubble will be different. My hair is coarse. Even with a bit of dulling, shaving with the ProGlide does not irritate my skin. I feel a few nicks and pulls here and there where it was absolute smoothness in the beginning but that is it. Still love it over the Excel razor I used before. Just a FYI, I apply a little bit of mineral oil to the blades after shaving to keep it clean, sharp, and rust-free.<br /><br />I mentioned that I was not sure about the FlexBall. I can say now that it isn't useful for me. My shaving technique has me holding the razor handle loosely with my fingers. This way, I adjust to the contours of my face at the handle with my hand rather than rely on the FlexBall and the leaf spring that is used as a pivot. Other persons who apply more pressure when they shave may find the FlexBall more useful.<br /><br />Overall, I love the ProGlide for its smooth, non-irritating shave. I am pretty sure I won't be going back to the Excel. ProGlide blades are more expensive than the Excel ones ($3 vs $1 per blade). But to me, a smooth shave that does not hurt my skin is worth the price premium.

It definitely takes some getting used to if you have never used a Fusion ProGlide. Word of advice, don't press too hard and let the blades work their magic! What about the FlexBall? The FlexBall technology is subtle. Honestly, compared to the amount it can swivel, I didn't see it swivel much. I'm guessing the amount of swivel will depend on your facial contours? For me, I'm really not sure if it made that much of a difference. End result - One of closest shaves I have had in a long time. As my wife would say, &#34;smooth like a baby's bottom&#34;. Pros: The closest shave I've had in a long time. Decent price for the actual razor (which is roughly $10). Sleek look and feel. All Fusion cartridges are compatible with this handle. Cons: Prices for the cartridges are a little out of my price range. I'm cheap but this shouldn't discourage those of you who are willing to make the investment! Overall this is a great product that I would be happy to recommend to anyone. Thanks again Gillette!

Again--felt very solid and well constructed. The color of the body is black with silver trim, plus the orange Flexball.<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #1,&#34; I did not shave for several days, so that I had a 3-day beard. I washed my face with cool water, left my face wet, then applied a smooth layer of the Proglide gel. I then waited several minutes for my beard to soften. I began shaving in the easier portions of my face, where the whiskers are lighter, then proceeded to the heavier sections around my chin. The razor nicely navigated all the crags and contours without the slightest drag or snagging. The blades cut very close without the hint of scraping or cutting. I examined my face very closely after shaving, and I was very pleased with the result. The razor did an outstanding job, providing a very close, clean shave. (For the records, I do NOT have a really smooth face--it's about normal roughness.)<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #2,&#34; I had just the normal 1-day beard. I washed my face with warm water, left my face wet, then similarly applied a layer of the same gel. I waited exactly 3 1/2 minutes for the bristles to soften. This time, I paid attention to how well the razor traversed over the chin and down to the neck. I wanted to see if the rotating head of the razor could smoothly navigate this hilly territory. As before the razor did a similarly outstanding job, providing a very close and smooth shave. Thus, both the Field Tests confirm the capability of this product. It works as advertised. When I completed my shaving, I rinsed the razor, and noticed that it is somewhat difficult to get the blades entirely clean of shaving gel. With 5 blades closely spaced together, this is not a trivial feat. After cleaning, I thoroughly dried the cartridge, as I hope to extend the life of the blades.<br /><br />▲ The famous &#34;Flexball&#34; is obvious because of its bright orange color. The Flexball pivots in 2 different ways. As you hold the razor in front of you, it pivots left to right, in an angular fashion--perhaps up to 15 degrees in each direction. There are little &#34;stops&#34; on the Flexball that prevent it from rotating too far. You can see a very fine band (at first I thought it was a wire) that allows the angular pivoting. This movement is very smooth--no hitches whatsoever. There is a small screw-like pivot-point, around which the movement takes place. This fastener appears to be very solid; I doubt anything will come lose. The head of the razor also pivots forward and back, using a thin &#34;bar&#34; going into the head of the razor.<br /><br />▲ The above Flexball is very impressive engineering. It appears to operate flawlessly. All of this is to allow the razor to match the contours of your face. That's a nice way of saying, shave around all those divots and dents in your face (not that YOU have any, of course, but someone else might.) To further get around those slight detours, this product uses extremely thin, five blades that are designed to glide more smoothly; thus, there is no tugging on your skin.<br /><br />▲ Gillette also claims to incorporate a proprietary strip called the &#34;Enhanced Lubrastrip.&#34; It's the part of the cartridge that is pale green. This strip contains mineral oil and &#34;lubricating polymers.&#34; Well, my skin appreciated those &#34;polymers.&#34;<br /><br />✔ SUMMARY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris LawsonY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris Lawson

So what does the Flexball Handle actually DO? Good question. The razors have tilted backward & forward to follow the contour of your face for literally at least a decade or more, right? The Flexball Handle essentially now allows it to curve not only up & down, but now left & right as well, giving your new razor unprecedented facial comfort and coverage. All this should translate into not only the best shave ever, but smoothest as well, right? In reality, I noticed absolutely ZERO difference in how close the razor shaved than my previous Proglide without the Flexball Handle.<br /><br />Now, let me be clear: I still LOVE the Proglide, and firmly believe that if I have the choice of using the Gillette versus pretty much every model of personal shaver available, I'll go with the Gillette pretty much every time (unless of course I cannot afford one, in which case I have 3 different and much cheaper models which I believe work easily 98% as good).<br /><br />To sum it up, I LOVE the Proglide--but don't see that the Flexball Handle works really any better than the regular model. Maybe that's because the regular Proglide works so well, that the difference is purely subjective to each user, I'm not entirely certain to be honest. All I know is it works, and works well...but if the Flexball is more expensive, I cannot endorse paying more. If they are the same price as the regular Proglides, then no problem. Otherwise, I'd stick with the regular razor.

My first shave with the new blades required just one pass over each area of my face and the end-result was the smoothest shave I have ever had—not having to pass over the same area multiple times made it an incredibly quick shave as well! I credit the lubrication strip included on the cartridges as well as the new shave gel which goes on smooth and easy. Throughout the entire shave I could feel the layer of protection that remained on my skin stroke after stroke—no nicks, cuts, or razor burn after using this product.<br /><br />Conclusion: the Fusion ProGlide FlexBall razor paired with ProGlide 2-in-1 shave gel is a package that lives up to all of the hype. Pricing on this shaving system, including refill cartridges, is comparable to other products but the value of what you get for your hard earned dollar goes further with Gillette. This combo of razor and gel is truly the best a man can get.
